The weapon types and effectiveness really depend on you as a player. While some people might find dodging and using a homing target gun good, others prefer the spread and charged shot. It reminds me of the original megaman, except instead of lives you take hits. The difficulty is akin to hitting your head against a wall, eventually breaking through and feeling like you achieved something. The 1930s Disney cartoon feel make me feel reinvigorated to try the boss again, and find more secrets on the map. The supers help, and everything has  a place. You can simply beat a boss, or try to get its soul contract at a higher difficulty. It pushes players to play better. If I had two gripes. They arent deal breakers just things that would have made bosses a million percent more fun is knowing how much damage you've done whether its cracks in a boss or a simple health bar it would make me feel like I can experiment with different weapons and see how I can knock a boss down easier. Second I want to play Mugman in Singleplayer. In any case having some cracks in a boss to show progress or a health bar would be nice but that said its a fantastic game and NEEDS to be in your library. Even with the difficulty I find the charm of the game overwhelming. 5/5

ArtificialRaven	Recommended	11.3	https://steamcommunity.com/id/artificialraven/	Cuphead is a fast paced arcade-style action platformer with a fantastic early 1900's cartoon art style and soundtrack. It sports single player & local co-op 2 player modes. Boasting some of the tightest controls I've ever felt in a 2D action platformer and subjectively some of the best looking authentic hand drawn animation in gaming, For me just the spectacle was worth the price of admission.  While difficult, the game consists of numerous boss fight stages and 6 platforming stages spread over the course of 4 worlds.  With the uber responsive controls, varied weapons, super moves and charms the player can purchase, the player is given all the tools needed to be succesful. Failure strictly lies with that of the player and not the game. It feels punishing but fair. So one must practice, practice and practice. Besides the boss & platforming stages there is a small, linear world map to explore with NPCs, shortcuts and hidden goodies along with a shop to spend your gold coins in to purchase upgrades.  Once you've defeated the bosses of each world you're allowed to move on to the next ultimately facing off with the Devil at the end. There are special unlockable color & sound modes for completing hidden objectives, such as beating all the Run 'n Gun (platforming) stages without killing a single enemy. And for getting a perfect grade on all platforming and boss stages. There's even an expert mode if players complete the game on Regular difficulty. The achievements will also feel satisfying and well earned.Is this worth the $20 USD price tag? I sure thought it was. My only regret was not buying the Deluxe Edition with the soundtrack. The game is short but sweet. Quality over quantity. That's it for my mini-review of Cuphead, thank you for reading.

The variety in the bosses is top notch, you'll be adjusting your strategies all over the place to try to survive. It was a long wait, holding out for this game to finally arrive but this is one game that lived up to and exceeded every expectation. StudioMDHR deserves all the success they get from this. 10/10 recommendation.

Xuchilbara	Recommended	63.8	https://steamcommunity.com/id/ryukthecreep/	Cuphead is a great game, a wonderful piece of handwork and a great homage to old-school gaming. It delivers a fun, demanding yet rewarding experience that cannot leave anybody indifferent thanks to its amazing art direction, animation and exquisite soundtrack. So it's all good, right? Well, not really...Lemme say that Cuphead's gameplay is very solid and the way it has been filled with references and homages to old classic games - like Super Mario, Megaman and Contra - is further proof that the developers know well what good game design is about. However, there are some flaws here and there that can be quite annoying, especially if you're trying to get perfect ranks. For instance, some levels like Perilous Pliers or bosses like Beppi the Clown involve a significant amount of randomness in attack patterns, which can often lead to situations where is nearly impossible to avoid getting hit. Another problem can be found in the way certain elements in the foreground are placed, which sometimes partially obscure visuals thus creating an utterly artificial and obnoxious obstacle for the player. Level and boss design is generally good, sometimes remarkable, aside for one big exception: Rumor Honeybottoms (aka the honeycomb boss). A vertical scrolling level where you are constantly being forced to jump off-screen and where 90% of the times you get hit are from something you cannot see, is just something I didn't want to find in a modern game. Especially not in a game like this.A minor complaint I have is about the "Simple" difficulty: personally I don't care about it because I always play levels on Regular or Expert, but from what I saw it seems rather pointless since you can beat bosses but it doesn't count them on your list, thus preventing you from finishing the game. I think that's just unfair for many people that want to try an accessible mode but ultimately find themselves cut off near the finishing line. If you want to include an easier difficulty you either do it properly or you don't do it at all.Another minor thing that bugs me is about the "Pacifist" rank in run n' gun levels: I think that there should have been separate rankings for completing a level with an A+ and for completing it with a P. As it is, the game considers the P ranking the highest so it's pretty useless to sweat yourâ™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥trying to get an A+ when you can just go straight for a pacifist run. That's rather nonsensical since when you're doing a pacifist run you don't have to worry about time, damage or parrys, hence it's much easier to do so than to make a perfect run.Finally, bugs: there are quite a few as you can see from the discussion thread in the forums, but I personally never found gamebreaking ones. The fact that there hasn't been a single patch since the release is not comforting though, and I hope that the devs will fix some issues that are currently preventing some people from playing the game.To conclude, I know I might sound quite critical in this review, but believe me when I say that this game is absolutely amazing and that I love it with passion. It's exactly for this reason that I wanted to highlight its weak points instead of just praising it, 'cause I think that StudioMDHR guys have the potential to make even more amazing games in the future and I really want them to learn from their (overall few) errors. That said, I highly recommend everyone to play this gem, enjoy it and let yourself be amazed by the crazy world of Cuphead - even if that means you'll have to swear to your monitor a bit. It will be worth your while.

It's nothing like Undertale or Donkey Kong Country (examples off the top of my head) but each track individually resinates perfectly with each boss, run 'n gun, just walking around and even in the store. It gives a warm welcoming feel to the environments.-It's hard. It's not a game you're gonna walk through easily in less than an hour, you will rage, you will get angry - but that's the beauty of Cuphead. It isn't just going to give you generic bosses and repeat them throughout the game. A kind of short game but compact with so many different elements all captured perfectly in every single level. It's hard, but it's not just hard for the sake of being hard like, for example, Dark Souls. It's hard to constantly challenge and push the player. You won't beat every boss within the first couple tries, it's going to take you a WHILE to figure out patterns for each boss.-The developers have clearly taken time and sunken hours into every little detail you will find, and you can tell instantly. Passion and care into every single individual aspect. -The storyline, it's not the most fascinating but it's straight to the point, you know exactly what's going on as soon as you start. It also fits in well to the 1930's cartoon style, this is something I could see being pulled straight from the likes of a cartoon from Max Fleischer. Even the bosses suit that era of cartoons where people would get their heads cut off, spooky skeletons everywhere and other absurd stuff that nowadays would get slandered by the mass media for being too "offensive".Cons:-There is a bug in the 2nd stage/world on Sugarland Shimmy where when you get to the final stage of the battle, you will never progress, when you die you will be stuck and unable to finish or beat the boss. If you try on the easier difficulty you can get to the end of the final stage but you won't be able to finish. You have to start over if you get it (I have not found a solution). Is has yet to be patched. -Some of the bosses rely purely on a set pattern so it kind of takes the fun out of facing them when you easily learn the pattern, I would of liked to see more bosses that are random in the sense that there is no pattern to what they do that can be learned, therefore making it easier (if that made sense I'm not sure. That's me nitpicking, this is a reletively flawless game, you can tell the dev team have worked incredibly hard to make this game as amazing as it is, which is refreshing since most companies usually opt for more money over making a solid game (Ark, H1Z1, CS:GO).9.4/10. xConsumed.by.FEARx	Recommended	9.1	https://steamcommunity.com/id/nevergiveuphope/	Well howdy-do-dee, folks! It's been like, what, 3 years since I decided to write a review on a game? Any game? Oh who am I kidding, you're here for Cuphead, aincha? And ever since this game's only got funny shÃŒtposts for the last week, let's get right into it, shall we?I rate it 10/10.Well that jumped from 0 to 100 really quick hasn't itOk, let me explain:This is a game you have to experience blind in order to enjoy all it has to give. While this review is meant to be spoiler-free, I highly encourage you purchase it right now, finish the game, and then come back here just to tell me "Jeez random reviewer, this game was pretty good!"I mean, none of you will say that, but you get what I mean.Now without furtherado- the review:What is this game? It's esentially a boss rush platformer with some run'n'gun levels added in. And of course, it has that 1930's cartoony style as its main premise. Now, why is that important...When it comes to games, GAMEplay comes first, then graphics. However, Cuphead is quite the enigma. When we talk about graphics, we usually have instant comparisons to other games in mind. But when we talk about a graphic fidelity truly unique and with no competitors on the market to this date, can we really say anything? Well I'll say something: it's fÃ¹cking beautiful.Y'see, when I was little, I always watched shows such as Tom and Jerry, Loony Tunes, and even some communist made cartoons(didn't see that one coming didja?) These cartoons were, simply put, the best. Now don't get me as a grumpy grandpa when you read this, the cartoons we have today are great!(Save for TTG) However, these are much more down to Earth than the medium that was from 80s(maybe even later) and forward that were all about these fantastic phenomenons: characters stretching limbs, turning into all sorts of present objects/items, the weak creature(a mouse, a rabbit) would always turn out victorious, that sort of thing,And this is where Cuphead just NAILS: It doesn't matter if it's based from 30's animation, it still catches what would be relatable to animation in both the world wars: a german rat in a tin can "tank", all sorts of day-to-day objects with limbs, eyes and personas, a god damn bee turning into a fokin plane bomber, the usual.And we have gone so far without even mentioning that the whole game(THE ENTIRITY OF IT) is hand drawn. Exactly as it was almost a century ago. And keep in mind this took 7 years to make(if I'm not mistaken), so that's not something everyone can do.Now enough chit-chat about the amazing graphics, what about the GAMEplay? Or actually, the story.The story is fitting, given the aesthetic and charm Cuphead goes for. You and your friend buy some lootboxes, then EA steps in and asks for one more purchase, and boom now your credit card is empty. Then EA felt sympathetic and tells you to hunt some Youtubers that owe them money and that's about it. Wait, that's not how the story goes... Ah fÃ¹ck it, ye get the idea. Now how about that sweet gameplayThe gameplay is servicable and it's pretty fun. You play as Cuphead or Mugman, respectively in local co-op, in order to gather the soul contracts for EAThe Devil. As you fight bosses and upgrade stuff, you get to customize your loadout: two weapons, one charm and one ultra. There are a total of 6 charms and weapons and 3 ultras. I've got to say they all do their job well, as for the weapons they always find at least one boss's weakness, and the charms more so stay to preference. I for one found the invincible dashing to be a lot more useful than an extra life. But each to their own. As for the ultras, essentially(God I said that a lot), as you do damage, you fill up a super meter which allows you to do a charged attack with your weapon that does more damage possibly maybe I think idk. Once your super meter is full, you activate your ultra, and all 3 of them have their use in the right circumstances. Now how about them bosses?The bosses are the bread and butter of this game and ye can't deny it. There is just so much variation and creativity going around all of them, I'm almost too scared to even spoil them. Actually, I'm not even gonna. Except to say that they catch the portrayal of a 30's cartoon spot on. That's it, that's all you're getting. Now for that sweet sound.The soundtrack is pretty much entirely just jazz, so if you're a fan of jazz, you'll instantly fall in love with the soundtrack, for it is gorgeous. Do you remember when you died over and over again on Super Meat Boy but you weren't all that frustrated since the music was rocking awesome? Well yeah, just imagine that into jazz and BOOM, there's your soundtrack.Now, the difficulty... it really shows just how casualized both the AAA and indie industry has gotten. People have gone so far to call this(THIS) the "Dark Souls of platformers". As to which I have to say: Just... how fÃ¹cking dense are you? If this is the Dark Souls of platformers you clearly have never heard in your pathetic life of The End is Nigh, N++, Spelunky, that japanese pedophile game, and so many other platformers that are considered difficult from stance of gameplay. THIS is how an average game should be like, not the sort of garbage Gone Home is like, where the game plays for itself and you cannot lose. Y'all remember that asian cÃ¹ntbag that calls himself journalist took him over 60 seconds to finish the tutorial? Goes to show how low we sunk, but to be fair, gaming outlets didn't have any standards to begin with.tl;dr Now to wrap up, or if you're only reading this, it's no spoiler as I mentioned it from square one that this game gets a 10/10. But why? Let me tell you why: outstanding graphic fidelity, challenging gameplay, original soundtrack and all around lots of fun to have on this indie masterpiece. Whereas games like Undertale absolutely sunk within the spam of 4 months, I don't see this receiving any hate anytime soon.This has been your round of the mill reviewer, and what are you doing, just play the game already.

THE END~~~~~~~Actual review~~~~~~~OK, the art style is nothing like the other games that you see. It's not 4k HDR or anything. It's just pretty, it's styled after the old timey cartoons. But with a fresh twist making the art style it's own. 9/10 graphics.The story is very simple. You make a deal, and loose it and do what the devil says. You get money from completing levels allowing more powers to make life a little better. But don't worry, you'll never find your self bored with the levels. It ramps up difficulty in a amazing way never making it easy on your first run (maybe more if your me). The story is simple, But it's not bad having a simple story, that's not how the game is, it's not centered around story.The reason this game is truely great is the gameplay. As stated earlier, this game is hard. to a point where taking breaks will actually help. And the weapons are very interesting. This game truelly feels like it's own game, and not a clone or heavily based off anything. Everything is built from the ground up, and you can tell. Even if you put 10 minutes into this game. You just know, from the controls, to the first level you play. This game is also great if you have freinds. Something I do not.score:9/10

If you see this on sale and you still don't have it, you should actually *wait* until it's full price before picking it up. It's that good.Perfect difficulty. Although this may be a point of contention for some, I believe difficulty vs. reward in this game is perfect. There's a simple mode that allows less experienced players have a shot at seeing most of the content. The regular difficulty is not that difficult. I'm pretty experienced at platformers, but I'm not that good. The game only took me roughly 7 hours to beat on regular on a blind playthrough. Compare that to a game like say "I wanna be the guy" and you'll find the difficulty and amount of time spent very reasonable.Variety. 20+ bosses, each with multiple phases and every single phase is unique. Not to mention multiple weapons, super powers and charms that allow you to brew your own flavor of Cuphead.Unique. I've never played an officially released game like this. I attempted to play "I Wanna Be The Guy" and failed miserably, but that game was never officially released. As far as I know, this is first of this type of game to be officially released. I could be and probably am wrong. But this was a wholly new and unique experience for me, and likely to many others who might pick this up. (Please tell me of other games if I am wrong, because I would love to play them!)Cons:Repetitive. This will flat out turn some people off. You will die many, many times in this game. You will hear the same music, play through the same boss phase, and hear the same sound effects a plethora of times consecutively. This can irritate a casual gamer, but in my opinion, that is where the aesthetic really helps. It's hard to stay mad at Woody Woodpecker stuck in a birdhouse.Casually Difficult. While there is a simple mode in this game, it will still be too much for some casual gamers. If they are not able to beat the first 3 or so levels, that's all they will see. This is true of most games, however. It just may be too difficult for your average casual gamer that may be interested in this art style/aesthetic. If you believe you are one of these people, it may be better to just watch someone play the game. It pains me to say that, but 20 bucks is 20 bucks.Somewhat short. This is a very small gripe, because it feels like there is so much content in this game. The playtime of 7 hours to casually beat the game on regular seemed a bit on the short end to me. Now, I plan on getting all of the achievements and even trying my hand at a speedrun, but for a first time playthrough, it left me wanting. This may have also been enhanced by, again, how truly unique and breathtaking the aesthetic is.I had to write a review for this game, because it's not often that a game comes along and wows you the way that this game did for me. 10/10 - An instant classic.

Some of the things are major and others minor. Sorry if I type something wrong in English. Graphics  99% sure most of the people noticed this game because of these gorgeous graphics. And I don't blame you. Really beautiful graphics and animations. It's a really good thing Studio MDHR put a lot of effort to this for multiple reasons.Beautiful graphics and animations are pleasent to look at -> People want to advance in the game and see what else developers made.It's always clear, when boss is about to attack (animation). In these kind of hectic games it's very important to have a clear indication, that the boss is about to do something. This way boss fights are fair.Guns having a "color code" helps player to notice what weapon they are using. Also bullets have different shapes so that helps as well. Audio Absolutely fantastic and fits the game perfectly. Even a metalhead like myself enjoys these jazz tunes!Good music keeps you going, even if you have died 100 times. Controls Controls feels really tight and I really don't have anything bad to say. Cuphead does exactly what I want him to do.Default control layout can feel a bit wonky, so I do recommend changing some inputs. Gameplay It's fun, challenging and rewarding. Everything I was expecting from this gameIn "Gun & Run" levels, if you dash forward really fast and multiple times, it can change enemies' spawning time/location. This only applies for people who maybe want to speedrun the game(?)There are some glitches, but let's be real, every game got some. If you want to see one I encountered, feel free to watch this clip from my stream -> https://clips.twitch.tv/MistyHelplessSashimi4HeadHitboxes are really fair, for the most part. I only encountered one boss, who got little bit of wonky hitboxes. Here is another clip from weird hitboxes -> https://clips.twitch.tv/YawningPrettiestEggplantFunRunI would like to add, that one small glitch or one weird hitbox from one boss didn't ruin my fun with the game. Final Verdict It took me around 22 hours to beat this game twice (regular difficulty & expert getting best ranks every stage) and I like this game so much, I might start speedrunning this. It's so good game. If you are looking for a challenging bossrush game with little bit of platforming, awesome music and beatiful graphics, I recommend this game for you.

Atrox	Recommended	49.8	https://steamcommunity.com/profiles/76561198058702996/	Cuphead may be one of my favorite games of the year. The 1930s Fleischer-esque style hooked me and the prospect of a meaty challenge only made me want to play it even more.I'll say this much, Cuphead is a challenging game, but it's not impossible or unfair. Most of the game is boss battles filled with various attack patterns to duck and weave while you chip away at the boss's health. It's easy to back yourself into a corner, but as long as you're smart about your positioning, the game always gives you a window of opportunity to avoid attacks.... it's just sometimes that window is very very small. This game will beat you down, but as long as you're tenacious and pay attention, you can only get better.Gameplay aside, the sheer amount of love and care put into this game shows in the artwork and music. Every sprite has been animated by hand tradtionally (animated with pencil and paper) as opposed to digitally (in a program like Photoshop or Flash) as seen in games like Skullgirls or Indivisible. The sprites were colored digitally to be brought into the game, but are processed in a way to give a genuinely aged film feel. There's enough gaming references to keep gamers happy (Sally's Divekicks, Ribby and Croaks doubling as a Street Fighter and Battletoads Mashup, Dr. Kahl's allusion to both Dr. Wily and Dr. Robotnik, etc), but also plenty of Golden Age cartoon references to keep the animation buffs happy. I feel like every boss, every stage has a connection to some old Fleischer, Iwerks, or Famous Studios short I've seen before, but without being carbon copies of any characters in those shorts. I can't be the only one that thought of Balloon Land when fighting Beppi the Clown. Or Somewhere in Dreamland while battling Baroness Von Bon Bon. I especially love the watercolor backgrounds, which not only reflect how backgrounds were made back then, but also make the animated characters (like you and the enemies) stand out. It's used to great effect on the overworld map, as the stages and things youi can interact with are slightly animated, appearing wobbly and lighter than other parts of the map. A great touch that works with this style but also works from a gameplay perspective. I'm still floored at how the Moldenhauers were able to make this all come together so naturally.The music is also incredible. The majority of tracks in the game are played by a full jazz band, and it hits a sweet spot between a style that suits the game's aesthetic, but also works to keep you focused on the game. The music is dynamic enough that the speed and pitch will change depending on if you use a super, pause or even die (where the music sort of dies down to a crawl). Great attention to detail. The musicians deserve as much credit as the artists.Cuphead's a great game, but it's not for everyone. Some people won't find the challenge or style all that fun or engaging. But for those who love a challenge, or are willing to go the distance to see more of the game's crazy art and animation, this is definitely the game for you.

Endyo	Recommended	5.1	https://steamcommunity.com/id/endyo/	Few things please me more in indie games than unique art styles executed well.  Cuphead leaps to the very top of my list of games that pull this off with near perfection.  But anyone would be able to derive that from a minute or two of video.  The real question is whether the game is actually fun to play, and luckily, the answer is yes â€“ but with some hurdles for your average player.A 1930s Walt Disney Fever DreamRight up front Cuphead impresses with a design and art style that is easily described as what an artist in the 1930s would create with the description of what a modern video game is supposed to be.  It truly looks and feels like it was plucked from a strange anachronistic timeline.  The designs and animations of every character could easily be transposed into old Warner Brothers cartoons and look right at homeâ€¦ and man are those designs something to behold.  The main protagonists, Cuphead and Mugman (the second playerâ€™s character that wonâ€™t be around playing solo), are unique in their own right, but they end up being the least interesting thing you encounter in the game.  Bosses transform multiple times for each encounter, offering up completely new visuals to go with their new set of abilities.  The vast majority are fanciful characters from the start, ranging from anthropomorphic vegetables to some sort of Zeppelin woman that transforms into a moon for some reason, and everything in between.   Thatâ€™s just in the first act.  It only gets wilder from there, but I wonâ€™t ruin the surprise trying to describe what turns out to be one of the more entertaining parts of the game.  It is actually quite easy to forget that even the backgrounds of these levels and boss fights are beautiful and have their own little animations.  I canâ€™t imagine the effort it took in developing this to seamlessly combine the animations with the gameplay.Indie Rage 2017The gameplay is where things are going to get a little feisty.  Iâ€™ve come to realize over the years that exceptionally difficult games end up leaving me feeling a little more sour than games where progress is consistent.  Retreading content is one of my least favorite things, whether itâ€™s backtracking in RPGs or having to restart a level or checkpoint because of something that comes out of nowhere.  Cuphead is without a doubt one of the toughest games Iâ€™ve played this year.  With most of the events in the game dumping straight into a boss fight, the game is generally referenced as a â€œboss rushâ€ title, though there are optional levels that are more traditional run and gun affairs that have you blasting away at tons of weak enemies in order to collect coins.  The coins are then used at a shop to unlock various different perks and weapons that are essentially sidegrades â€“ upgrading one attribute and downgrading another.  So you may get a weapon that has a unique attribute like a wide angle of damage, but if has a shorter range.   However, being able to carry two at a time and switch between them means you can set a loadout specific for a tough boss fight in order to make it a little easier on you.  With the game being as tough as it is, thereâ€™s not really a way to make it appeal to everyone.  I know I raged several times and even said aloud to my monitor that a particular boss or level was unfair, but every time Iâ€™ve gone to war against one of these â€œunfairâ€ things, Iâ€™ve managed to overcome it to great relief.  Cuphead manages to be equal parts immense frustration and gratifying success thanks to each boss fight being a matter of minutes at most.  In some ways, it works out like Super Meat Boy with its quick turnaround, meaning even when you fail repeatedly on a boss, you end up trying many more times because itâ€™s just a quick button press and youâ€™re back in at the start of the fight.   At first, I was a bit disappointed that the game didnâ€™t feature the rich and extensive level design of a game like Megaman, despite sharing a lot of the core jumping and shooting side scroll gameplay, but I found the numerous unique boss battles to be even better than those youâ€™d find in the classic blue bomber series.  The part where I recommend itDifficulty alone wouldnâ€™t be enough to make me hesitate to recommend this to nearly everyone.  Itâ€™s really a marvelous piece of work that just radiates its quality of craftsmanship.  I havenâ€™t even completed the game because the frustration leads me to putting it down at relatively short intervals, but I keep coming back and wanting to make it just a little bit further to see what silly animated bits of nostalgia will be presented.  I think that it might turn off people who are not at least a marginal fan of platformers, but if you were a fan of Megaman, Contra, or any classic platformer with shooting, youâ€™ll probably have enough experience to enjoy the gameplay and also get the treat of seeing a developer raise the bar on creativity.  I can only hope that Studio MDHR plans to make a sequel or at least another game featuring this fun aesthetic, because they really seem to know what theyâ€™re doing despite not having any previously released games as a company.If you'd like to see more of my reviews, check out my curator page here: http://steamcommunity.com/groups/EndyoGaming#curation

MrNergles	Recommended	31.3	https://steamcommunity.com/id/MrNergles/	TL;DR - Cuphead is a seriously great game, for many reasons, but everything aside the gameplay is what keeps bringing me back.  If you have $20 to burn on a game and you like a solid challenge, addicting gameplay with tight controls you should seriously buy this product. If it ends up too hard or not what you want in games use the Steam Refund; I do ask of you to try and soldier through it because losing is part of the fun. Go try out Gunstar Heroes, Dynamite Headdy, Contra 3, Alien Soldier or another ShmUp/Run&Gun first on an emulator if you aren't sure about the game. Also, use a controller. Couch only co-op, you can play online using a 3rd party app.I am running this game on Windows 10 with a GeForce GTX 870M NVidia card. Playing through this game I used a Mortal Kombat X (X360/X1) fight controller.Review: This game is as welcoming as it comes to anyone looking for a challenge and ready to learn some patterns. Being a huge fan of hand animation and classic Run&Gun games this is my niche. The boss rush and jump/shoot/avoid style approach a type of game that isn't produced often anymore; with that being said the difficulty that this game brings to the table isn't produced often either. This difficulty isn't for the light hearted; you will die, try again and die some more. It resembles the old style of games it is trying to emulate perfectly to the point where it becomes it's own monster. The closest thing this game comes to hand holding is giving you a small hi-five on the tutorial stage. With that being said the game is pretty accessible if you have the focus and the level headedness to learn the patterns in the many tries it takes for you to beat the boss. Patterns are important to this game, without putting the pieces together over a few tries you won't be able to put together the puzzle the level is trying to convey to you. This creates a great personal value for the game and makes you think and learn about the level's design! But if you plan on taking this game on you need to learn the controls.The controls on this game are very tight, they give you so much control that it's easy to lose control of Cuphead/Mugman. I mean that in the best way though, you just forget that they turn on a dime or dash as soon as you tap that button so when you get in a sticky situation it feels unfair but you are the only one to blame. It happens but once you start to understand you can become one with the machine. Moving and dashing aren't the only thing that feels natural to the player, the jumping sensitivity and shooting feel amazing as well as rewarding. All of this being said I do not recomend your keyboard this game was made with a controller in mind, you can bind all keys to whatever you want no matter what you use to play though.Using these tight controls and facing the difficulty/patterns don't really mash up until you add the levels into the mix. The levels are amazing spanning from 19 unique bosses (More if you count King Dice's fight individually) and 6 Run & Gun levels. These bosses are played in a platforming style except 5 of them that are done in a ShmUp style. This creates a nice balance of diversity in a condensed game. Adding to the diversity of each level the game is designed in an amazing Rubber Hose animation style with eye popping color and music true to the era and mood; creating a great experiance for the player. Each level is introduced with it's own episode card which adds a little extra spice to this difficult, fun and aestheticly pleasing burrito. For each burrito there is an end and with that being said would you order that same item again? For Cuphead the answer is yes. The game has an extremely high replay value from Expert Mode, Co-Op, Unlockables/Secrets and it you want to go ham learning those patterns to speedrun! Whether it is wrapping up over world requests from NPC's or destroying a boss with a friend you'll have a lot of fun. The only gripe I have about co-op is that it is couch co-op only, which I understand why but a boy can dream. The final thought's I will leave you on about this game is that this game while being insanely fun, challenging and beautifully put together with the handmade animation/originally composed & preformed music this game won't be for everyone. It's a painfully hard game for anyone to just jump in unless you've spent a lot of time around these type of games or have been playing for a few hours. It really bummed me out I couldn't share this game with my father who loves this animation and music(Someone who han't touched a controller since SNES) other than him watching it for a moment. Its a game that will be discouraging to someone like that. That being said to the people who can take on the challenge or want to learn this game is a clear cut perfect game that you should buy. $20 dollar for this product is criminally low and I am surprised it hasn't been raised to $35-$45 because it is honestly worth that or even more. You get a lot of value for that price. This is one of the best video games I have played for a very long time and has made it's way to my heart extremely fast breaking into my Top 10. 5/5

JDEzekude	Recommended	14.2	https://steamcommunity.com/id/mysteryezekude/	Cuphead is a beautifully intense run-and-gun platformer that pays homage to the Golden Age of Animation (e.g. 1930s Disney and Fleischer) and puts your reflexes to the test in a wacky cross between Mega Man and Gunstar Heroes.In this perilous cartoon adventure, you play as Cuphead and/or Mugman on a mission to collect wayward souls after losing a bet with the Devil himself. Thus, you will be pitted against over 20 crazy bosses, each with their own unique design and attack patterns.Throughout this journey, you'll be armed with one or two weapons at a time (which can be shot in 8-directions), a Megaman-X-style dash, a mid-jump parry (for absorbing and/or operating pink objects) and a Super button for pulling off special moves.Each separate boss battle usually lasts 2-5 minutes, but every second counts. In each battle, you must take down the boss without losing all your health points (i.e. 3 minimum, 5 maximum), or else you'll have to start the fight from the beginning. Thankfully, you have infinite lives, so there's no need to worry about dying too many times.Regardless, it can be both frustrating and maddening to lose repeatedly to the same boss, especially when you get so close to beating it. If that weren't enough, each time you lose, the game even shows you how close you are to beating it, accompanied with the boss mocking you. But, on the brighter side, it makes the joy of finally overcoming said boss all the more satisfying. Never before have I experienced this feeling so many times in one game.This game also features 6 tricky platforming stages in which you can collect coins to spend on unlockable weapons (e.g. spread fire, charge shot, etc.) and charms (e.g. 1-2 extra health points, invincible dash, etc.). These stages are a nice change of pace from the onslaught of boss battles. You can also find hidden coins by exploring certain places and carrying out certain tasks on the world map.I personally had high hopes for this game ever since its teaser came out, and the final product has exceeded my expectations with its combination of fluid hand-drawn animation and toughs-as-nails action gameplay. Because of this, it was hard for me to be angry no matter how many times I failed at one boss or another.For me, this game's greatest strength is that it entices its players to keep trying and trying again until they win. And, after you finally triumph over a boss and feel the ecstatic joy of victory, it's then a matter of testing yourself to do better.However, this could've been a perfect game if it had more game modes than just its main story (i.e. lots of boss battles, a few platforming stages), particularly a survival mode or one or more competitive 2-player modes (e.g. race, shooting gallery, etc.). This game features 3 unique stages in which you must parry waves of pink ghosts from an urn in order to unlock a super special move. Unforunately, once you've completed each stage, you can never play them again (unless you start a new game). It would've been nice if this game had an endless mode with those stages in mind, because it would make the perfect break from the usual running and gunning.So, all-in-all, I consider "Cuphead" a colorful rollercoaster of cartoon carnage that will make you laugh, shout, cry and cheer from start to finish (as it made me and many others). Brace yourselves, casual and hardcore gamers alike, you'll be in for a bumpy ride that you'll never forget!

If you don't know, you're about to know what it is.-"Rubber hose animation was the first animation style that became standardized in the American animation industry. The defining feature of the style is "rubber hose limbs" â€” arms, and sometimes legs, that are typically simple, flowing curves, without articulation (no hinged wrists or elbows).[1]" Wikipedia 2017. So basically everything is rubbery and loose. So the limit to what you can draw is, well, there isn't one. And with this style of animation, it flows like water. But anyway, characters that are drawn with rubber hose are never seen standing still. They keep on bobbing and moving. And Cuphead is no exeption. They also overreact ALOT. And yet again, Cuphead nails it! Though the bad thing, is the process of drawing and animating rubber hose AND THEN putting it into a video game. (A decently long one at that) You need to DRAW it on paper, then draw the same thing but a tiny difference in movement that you want it to then repeat the process. Then they had to give it to people to digitally paint it and then put it all together. But it was all worth it for this amazing game! Love it <3.Gameplay:Cuphead is a Run n' Gun and boss game. You need to beat every boss in the world or Inkwell Island in Cuphead's case to progress. You can also purchase ability's that will help you by doing run n' gun stages or finding them in Inkwell islands. The stroyline is the two boys, Cuphead and Mugman, accidently found them selves in the devil's casino on a win streak. Then the devil comes and gives them a deal. "Win the next roll and all the loot in the casino is yours, but if you fail, your souls are mine!" They lose the bet and try to get out of it. The devil says he will let them go if they collect his soul contracts. Then off they go. As the internet says, Cuphead has a reputation of being REALLY HARD. A kinda great that will make you jump and yell, YESSSSSSS FINALLY I CAN ACTUALLY DO SOMETHING YEAHHHH!!!!!!!!!! Overall:It is a very good game! The best in the whole era of gaming! With it's animation that is so satisfying, and it's gameplay intense also pared with the sound and music makes you go from having the worst day ever, to seeing a double rainbow, finding a four leaf glover and then winning the lotterly!! It's barley priced to! So you should get it NOW. 10/10.

JDEzekude	Recommended	14.2	https://steamcommunity.com/id/mysteryezekude/	Cuphead is a beautifully intense run-and-gun platformer that pays homage to the Golden Age of Animation (e.g. 1930s Disney and Fleischer) and puts your reflexes to the test in a wacky cross between Mega Man and Gunstar Heroes.In this perilous cartoon adventure, you play as Cuphead and/or Mugman on a mission to collect wayward souls after losing a bet with the Devil himself. Thus, you will be pitted against over 20 crazy bosses, each with their own unique design and attack patterns.Throughout this journey, you'll be armed with one or two weapons at a time (which can be shot in 8-directions), a Megaman-X-style dash, a mid-jump parry (for absorbing and/or operating pink objects) and a Super button for pulling off special moves.Each separate boss battle usually lasts 2-5 minutes, but every second counts. In each battle, you must take down the boss without losing all your health points (i.e. 3 minimum, 5 maximum), or else you'll have to start the fight from the beginning. Thankfully, you have infinite lives, so there's no need to worry about dying too many times.Regardless, it can be both frustrating and maddening to lose repeatedly to the same boss, especially when you get so close to beating it. If that weren't enough, each time you lose, the game even shows you how close you are to beating it, accompanied with the boss mocking you. But, on the brighter side, it makes the joy of finally overcoming said boss all the more satisfying. Never before have I experienced this feeling so many times in one game.This game also features 6 tricky platforming stages in which you can collect coins to spend on unlockable weapons (e.g. spread fire, charge shot, etc.) and charms (e.g. 1-2 extra health points, invincible dash, etc.). These stages are a nice change of pace from the onslaught of boss battles. You can also find hidden coins by exploring certain places and carrying out certain tasks on the world map.I personally had high hopes for this game ever since its teaser came out, and the final product has exceeded my expectations with its combination of fluid hand-drawn animation and toughs-as-nails action gameplay. Because of this, it was hard for me to be angry no matter how many times I failed at one boss or another.For me, this game's greatest strength is that it entices its players to keep trying and trying again until they win. And, after you finally triumph over a boss and feel the ecstatic joy of victory, it's then a matter of testing yourself to do better.However, this could've been a perfect game if it had more game modes than just its main story (i.e. lots of boss battles, a few platforming stages), particularly a survival mode or one or more competitive 2-player modes (e.g. race, shooting gallery, etc.). This game features 3 unique stages in which you must parry waves of pink ghosts from an urn in order to unlock a super special move. Unforunately, once you've completed each stage, you can never play them again (unless you start a new game). It would've been nice if this game had an endless mode with those stages in mind, because it would make the perfect break from the usual running and gunning.So, all-in-all, I consider "Cuphead" a colorful rollercoaster of cartoon carnage that will make you laugh, shout, cry and cheer from start to finish (as it made me and many others). Brace yourselves, casual and hardcore gamers alike, you'll be in for a bumpy ride that you'll never forget!

Â¤ Î²â„“Ð¾Ð¾Ä‘Ñ‡ Â¤ Nico-Kun!	Recommended	12.3	https://steamcommunity.com/id/Nico-Kun/	Cuphead is a fantastic 2D platformer with a beautiful, hand-drawn art-style that gives it a lot of charm. The game's story is presented in a way that's reminiscent of old cartoons (think Tom & Jerry, or early Looney Toons), and the art style itself further enhances this; it actually feels as if you were playing one of those cartoons.So, what's the story about? It's about two kids, Cuphead and Mugman, who get in trouble after dealing with the Devil, and now they have to fight the Devil's debtors in order to retrieve their souls. Anyway, it's all an excuse to travel around different levels beating the ever-lovingâ™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥of a bunch of colourful enemies.As far as the gameplay goes, it's fantastic. Like I said in the opening paragraph, it plays like a 2D platformer, although that's kind of a misnomer, since most of the stages actually consist of boss battles, with only a handful of platforming stages. The controls are pretty good, and you have several upgrades that you can acquire through a shop, or special stages. The game is pretty difficult for a newcomer, but not in the sense that it becomes frustrating to play; the fact that most stages are over pretty quickly, and that you get to see how much progress you made through the stage when you die encourages you to keep playing. (YouTube)Dragnix	Recommended	11.2	https://steamcommunity.com/id/Dragnix/	 Target Audience:   Those who don't want a walk in the park, also art fans Summary:  Despite the target audience above, saying that Cuphead is this revolutionary difficult game is a little misleading. Not in a gaming industry with japanese SHMUPs thats for sure. But Cuphead will kill you over and over again: and that's alright. It's a game that relies on pattern/attack recognition and clawing your way further and further to the end of a boss. The combat mechanics are simple yet effective: as you have a limited set of moves and weapons to work with: but enough to change up  your strategy just enough to deal with specific bosses. Speaking of which, bosses all are unique and aren't altered versions of prior ones. Each battle teaches you something to use in your arsenal, and you have to adapt that lesson to the next ones. Hell, you may even need to throw it away if needed.This is all held together by a presentation that had a LOT of effort put into it....and it shows. The hand drawn characters without digital effects (ok, coloring, but really that's it) must have taken ages to do. But the end result is some of the cleanest animation you've ever seen in a video game, as the ccartoons look as authentic as they possibly could be for emulating the 1930s. The over the top nature of the presentation tells you a lot about all these various bosses without forcing exposition down your throat. And the music and sound design is pretty brilliant, able to emphasize the right parts of gameplay while not emphasizing what you don't need to pay immediate attention to. Where the game falls short for me in that next level of gameplay. The structure of the game is at the core of this problem: once you've mastered a boss, you may get a slight addition to the challenge in expert mode, but not a lot of replayability beyond that. Sure, you'll die a bunch, but it's not like the game requires a lot of skill to get past all of these challenges. Some yes, but not the hand eye coordination of a gaming god. I just, I don't know, I was expecting another layer, something to bring out more of the game when all was said and done. It's not the Game of the Year, not in a year where there's so many top level games coming out. It's just a cut under the top games of 2017, but it's still worth an immediate buy.Video Review:  https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Gv0I52LnZ5s Lists: Positives:  The hand-drawn presentation shows all the effort and love put into it. Characters come to life on the screen.  Animations are top notch. Some of the best animations in video games: indie or AAA.   The Sound design puts the emphasis on gameplay: warning you of the hazards that you don't see first, then going down the line. Controls are exactly what you need for this speed of gameplay: not too loose, not too tight. Just right. Music captures the era of the cartoon perfectly, keeping the action upbeat and jiving throughout the game. Learning mechanisms put on display here and are well implemented.  Simple gameplay works well for the space and battlefield in question.  Bosses hit good strategy variety, forcing you to adapt to them without feeling repetitive. Parry system gives good risk/reward for the most part. Extra weapon options actually give you benefits that are really useful in certain battles, and aren't just straight upgrades. One more run gameplay makes you want to overcome your foes without (for the most part) wanting you to throw your controller against the wall. Negatives: Once you learn a boss's tricks, you pretty much know what to do. The random element doesn't play that big part of the game. They built a really interesting set of characters and world...which leaves you wanting more in terms of the story.  The parry sequence on the dice boss needs some way of allowing you to practice.  Once you beat the game, I lost the feel to want to go back and try them again. The keyboard controls just don't compare to the controller. In fact, I'd go so far as to say that you have to play with a controller. It's just so much better.

Oshwah	Recommended	8.3	https://steamcommunity.com/id/BEANO/	The Positive: Cuphead is a BEAUTIFUL game. The graphics, the sound, the music - are completely accurate to what a 1930's cartoon would be in the day, and I've seen my fair share. The story is classic-feeling and (again) something a 1930's era cartoon would be about, and it's not complex. The price is fair, and there's no BS like in-game DLC, loot boxes, or the other junk that companies like *COUGH* [MOSTLY ALL OF THEM NOW] add to their games in order to repeatedly try and tap your wallet. The controls are basic and not overly-complex (I cover more on this - see "The Mixed" below) and the tutorial is fast and covers them quickly and makes you aware of what you need to know in order to progress through the game - which isn't too many. Overall, I think the developers did a great job and focused on the aspects that many companies sadly overlook - the gameplay. The level navigation, progression, and design is diverse and well thought-out. The only bug I found was a graphic that didn't disappear when it should have - the "crying tears" of the 'onion boss' didn't disappear after I had defeated it, and it remained during the rest of the level. However, I was only able to produce it once time and it didn't affect the gameplay.The Mixed: While the game is themed around a 1930's cartoon, don't let the cartoon-style looks fool you - this game is BLOODY DIFFICULT! You can lower the difficulty down a notch but only on the battle-styled levels, not on the "gun and run" stages. The controls aren't complex and neither are the number of moves you're required to learn in order to play, but you better memorize them and you better become a master at which key does which, or you're not progressing at all. You press the X key instead of the Shift key and make a mistake, you're not finishing the level and you're better off just selecting "RETRY" in the pause menu and starting over. I don't count this as a negative, as I love challenges and I can't knock a game down because of that. This difficulty can be disheartening for some and motivating for others. However, I feel that when I play, there's a big frustration factor that the difficulty absolutely plays into. I'll play for one hour and exit the game having not progressed a single level. However, it's not frustrating to the level that I stop playing - I find myself coming back after taking a break and having at it some more. I will say this, however: I feel that I am progressing through the game partially by mastering the controls, but also because I'm memorizing exactly how the level plays and when I should move, jump, shoot, or dash. Again, I'm mixed on the difficulty. I feel that if I could knock the difficulty down a notch on all stages and take a lower score, the game would appeal to those who just want to play and without yelling a curse word after dying for the 10th time on the same level.The Negative: Pretty much nothing. The only thing I call BS on is how I'll attempt to hit a pink object and it'll occasionally both count as a "success" (as in I successfully hit the object) and also count as a "hit" (meaning that the object hit me and knocks off 1 HP). It's miniscule and really not worth mentioning as a negative, but sorry - if you're going to make a game this difficult, you should expect people to call you out on things like that. Other than this, that's pretty much it.

IamDinosaur	Recommended	24.3	https://steamcommunity.com/id/aurealis-san/	Developer: Studio MDHRGenre: Run and Gun, Platform and Boss RushRelease Date: September 29 2017"It's time for a world class bout, now GO!" - The Devil speaks itself after the countdownSummary:Cuphead is a run and gun game, created by small indie company Studio MDHR. The game was originally announced back in E3 2014 but it was delayed because they needed more time to polish the game. It is safe to say that this game delivered way beyond expectation, like seriously, give these guys a round of applause for their greatest work and deserve a recognition. I will address some negative reviews later because it is irritating me. So let's talk about Cuphead in depth.Story:It is a tale of Cuphead and Mughead. Two boys are having fun and wondering around the map until they discover The Devil's Casino. Cuphead and Mughead decide to gamble and they are on a winning streak. Until the Devil himself appeared, he makes a proposition; if the Cuphead and Mughead wins the gamble, they are going to take the casino and everything, if they lose; their souls will be consumed by the Devil. Cuphead decides to be greedy and they lose the bet, meaning that their souls will be taken but they want to live instead. So they make another proposition from them. The Devil wants the Soul Contracts and they are in deep trouble once they got kicked out. Luckily, the Elder Kettle will help you out and do what the Devil says.Gameplay:The gameplay of Cuphead is very simple yet effective. It really reminds me of run and gun games like Contra series or should I say Contra-esque gameplay. The game provides an open world exploration but it is linear, that doesn't mean it's not a bad thing since it's supposed to capture the aesthetics of the game or more like what if there's a video game in 1930s. They added an upgrade system and you spend coins to buy shot types (spreads, charged shots, etc.) and charms (extra lives, supers regeneration, etc.) There is a parry system and it is intuitive to use. It is not a traditional parry like Dark Souls (lmfao), it is a visual cue (any pink projectiles or enemies). The controls are tight and customisable which is a great additional in case of everyone wants to have their own controls. It's easy to pick up the controller and master the mechanics. Every boss fights are unique and I love each bosses (even though it made me cry internally when I almost kill every bosses in the game). Cuphead implemented Co-Op during the playthrough, but unfortunately the game does not support online and I am not against it.Technical Aspect:The setting sets in 1930s like I mention on Gameplay paragraph. They absolutely capture the jazz musical scores, the animation of every single characters (I can't believe it's a frame by frame animation), the lively background during boss fights. The musical score and graphics, they are a 10 out of 10 rating. I was actually humming some boss fight's theme and they are catchy as. I love the references they add, like Acme from Looney Tunes or other things that is related to 1930s cartoon shows.Address to the Negative Reviews:I am going to address the negative reviews, so bear with me. Cuphead is challenging and fair, not impossible and difficult. This is what the game is meant to be played. The game throws back to the 90s platform run and gun shooter and boss rushes game. It helps you to be a perfectionist or getting better at it. I know people are sick of getting killed over and over again, but let me say this, it helps you to analyze what you did wrong on certain sections and improve it. Seriously, negative reviews are making me cringe because people say how lazy the difficulty is and the gameplay isn't too deep or repetitive. I know there is one saying; looks can be deceiving and this is the game that works out too well. I think that should wrap up this address.Verdict:Cuphead is one of the best indie platform run and gun game I have ever played for a while. The story seems basic but it didn't hold me back anyway. The gameplay is Contra-esque, which is fun for me. The musical scores, graphics and settings are â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥ing amazing. I hate to say this, Cuphead is not for everybody because of the difficulty but still give this game a try, it's a great game to start playing the difficult game genre. The bugs in this game are somewhat minimal, so I do not think there are any game breaking bugs I encountered so far. The official score for this game, a 9 out of 10.

Purpsâ„¢	Recommended	3.5	https://steamcommunity.com/id/Butt_Ghost/	Oh hey, Cuphead. It's got serviceable platforming shooter mechanics and a charming artstyle that keeps you invested trying to fight your way through to just to see the rest of the content and ......It's kinda boring, honestly. It's in this sorta place where the boss mechanics and attack patterns that take up most of the game aren't really that difficult compared to harder platformers that came before it, and what is difficult is the single life three hitpoint limit imposed on every level. The difficulty comes down to learning and perfectly executing not-all-that-hard segments of a bossfight that turn into a test of endurance when they're strung together. Bossfights also begin to randomize some elements, making you perfect even more segments until you either get all of them down perfect or (more likely) just have the randomized elements happen in the right order to make the easiest run. I got up to the third island - that I've heard is the last hub in the game before the final boss - in roughly 2 hours and haven't really felt any urge to play it since. Nothing about fighting the bee lady over and over for example has me so enthralled that I can't wait to get back to it, I'm not on the edge of my seat every time I drop from a randomized scrolling platform to dodge a fast but predictable projectile. Don't get me wrong, the mechanics are entertaining since they're well executed in the context of the genre they're in, but losing to the bosses over and over doesn't get me worked up and motivated like it does in other hard games like Devil May Cry/Bayonetta, Contra/Hard Corps or DoDonPachi because the game doesn't do much to make the fights anything but mechanically sterile and repetitive. Instead, repeating content over and over to get a mistake-free run just makes me feel tired. Beating bosses is less of a "YEAH, I DID IT!" and more of a "â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥, finally. What's next?" and I'd say that's owed mostly to the fact that doing a winning run feels pretty much exactly the same as the doing any of the runs that preceded them, just I didn't get hit by the thing by accident this time around. Cthulhu's Gribbly Monocle	Recommended	11.1	https://steamcommunity.com/id/shinwa/	Score: 8.5 / 10Price/Value: -$20Time: 11 Hours (Including A+ time)Difficulty: Completed Regular, working through ExpertActual Difficulty: Minor / ModerateInput Used: Keyboard & ControllerCuphead is a wonderful delight in it's animation and nostaIgic melodies; a somewhat challenging colourful action platformer in the guise of a 1930's children's cartoon. As mentioned above, Cuphead is an action platformer focused around two types of stages: Run n' Gun & multi-form boss fights. Many gamers of experience will immediately compare Cuphead's gameplay to that of Contra, Metal Slug & Mega Man; as the controls are incredibly tight - both on controller AND keyboard. I will comment that the game does become something of a cakewalk when a controller is used, making keyboard controls another layer of challenge. Recommend the standard W,A,S,D configuration. Difficulty, let's address it and the hype. Is this game as brutal and punishing as many claim it to be? No, not in the slightest. I have certainly played far more challenging titles of a similar nature in my life and the keys to success in Cuphead are the following: PATIENCE & PATTERN RECOGNITION. This game is beatable and can be a delight in the process; I'm looking forward to completing Expert - which seems incredibly simlar to Regular, just with a slight speed increase and weapon power decrease.Upgrades come in the form of: Super Abilities, Shot Types and Off-hand Charms. Super Abilities are just that, SUPER abilites! These are ready for use when your super meter at the bottom left of the screen is full charged. Being three in total - a horizontal attack, temporary invincibility and a form of mega cuphead tornado - I found myself sticking to the first.Shot Types are classics from NES/SNES games of old: Spread, lobber, hookshot, homing, etc. You purchase these from the shop and equip them as you please - two at a time - before entering a stage. A little trial and error will help you figure out the best combination for each stage.Off-hand Charms are many, but I used only one 'Smoke Bomb'. This allows you to dodge with an invincibility effect through enemies; incredibly handy.A delight from start to finish; decades old gamers will find a gem here that will remind them of games from their own childhood in the skin of our cartoons. Highly recommended.

http://funwithsauce.com/	Recommended	2.8	https://steamcommunity.com/id/AsoftDolphinn/	Product received for free
ð•Ÿð•¦ð•”ð•ð•–ð•’ð•£ ð••ð•™ð•’ð•£ð•žð•šð•¤ð•¥	Recommended	12.9	https://steamcommunity.com/profiles/76561198041596430/	Absolutely fantastic game all round- the art style / development techniques, the soundtrack, the gameplay, the narrative, all of it! However, there is one boss, which is fundamentaly flawed due to a number of factors, that I think should be redesigned. This is the Honeycomb Herald.To start, the fight is a vertical autoscroller; this in itself is already a poor design choice as the standard monitor's aspect ratio obviously favours the horizontal- allowing for time to see incoming projectiles and react accordingly as the screen forces you along. When it's vertical, however, there is little to no time to react, especially when sprites fly at you from out of view thanks to this orientation and can often just hit you after being on the screen for less than half a second.Secondly, dealing with platforms in a fluid and responsive manner (moving between both up and down) has always been a problem in platformers. When this is made even more difficult by the RNG of platform placement while the game is forcing you upwards, and there isn't sufficient vertical screen space to see if there will be platforms or not, it just makes for an annoying experience that is nigh-on impossible for the player to navigate around tactically without just a good pattern from luck.The RNG of the projectiles / enemies in combination with all this just makes for a complete mess.Overall, all of these aspects made this boss fight straight up un-fun. Unlike other bosses where they were frustrating, but the fault was entirely down to player error and the fights themselves were still enjoyable, as well as rewarding when beaten. Again, fantastic game all round, but that one boss was an unfortunate blemish on an otherwise incredible experience.

ð•Ÿð•¦ð•”ð•ð•–ð•’ð•£ ð••ð•™ð•’ð•£ð•žð•šð•¤ð•¥	Recommended	12.9	https://steamcommunity.com/profiles/76561198041596430/	Absolutely fantastic game all round- the art style / development techniques, the soundtrack, the gameplay, the narrative, all of it! However, there is one boss, which is fundamentaly flawed due to a number of factors, that I think should be redesigned. This is the Honeycomb Herald.To start, the fight is a vertical autoscroller; this in itself is already a poor design choice as the standard monitor's aspect ratio obviously favours the horizontal- allowing for time to see incoming projectiles and react accordingly as the screen forces you along. When it's vertical, however, there is little to no time to react, especially when sprites fly at you from out of view thanks to this orientation and can often just hit you after being on the screen for less than half a second.Secondly, dealing with platforms in a fluid and responsive manner (moving between both up and down) has always been a problem in platformers. When this is made even more difficult by the RNG of platform placement while the game is forcing you upwards, and there isn't sufficient vertical screen space to see if there will be platforms or not, it just makes for an annoying experience that is nigh-on impossible for the player to navigate around tactically without just a good pattern from luck.The RNG of the projectiles / enemies in combination with all this just makes for a complete mess.Overall, all of these aspects made this boss fight straight up un-fun. Unlike other bosses where they were frustrating, but the fault was entirely down to player error and the fights themselves were still enjoyable, as well as rewarding when beaten. Again, fantastic game all round, but that one boss was an unfortunate blemish on an otherwise incredible experience.

Xuchilbara	Recommended	63.8	https://steamcommunity.com/id/ryukthecreep/	Cuphead is a great game, a wonderful piece of handwork and a great homage to old-school gaming. It delivers a fun, demanding yet rewarding experience that cannot leave anybody indifferent thanks to its amazing art direction, animation and exquisite soundtrack. So it's all good, right? Well, not really...Lemme say that Cuphead's gameplay is very solid and the way it has been filled with references and homages to old classic games - like Super Mario, Megaman and Contra - is further proof that the developers know well what good game design is about. However, there are some flaws here and there that can be quite annoying, especially if you're trying to get perfect ranks. For instance, some levels like Perilous Pliers or bosses like Beppi the Clown involve a significant amount of randomness in attack patterns, which can often lead to situations where is nearly impossible to avoid getting hit. Another problem can be found in the way certain elements in the foreground are placed, which sometimes partially obscure visuals thus creating an utterly artificial and obnoxious obstacle for the player. Level and boss design is generally good, sometimes remarkable, aside for one big exception: Rumor Honeybottoms (aka the honeycomb boss). A vertical scrolling level where you are constantly being forced to jump off-screen and where 90% of the times you get hit are from something you cannot see, is just something I didn't want to find in a modern game. Especially not in a game like this.A minor complaint I have is about the "Simple" difficulty: personally I don't care about it because I always play levels on Regular or Expert, but from what I saw it seems rather pointless since you can beat bosses but it doesn't count them on your list, thus preventing you from finishing the game. I think that's just unfair for many people that want to try an accessible mode but ultimately find themselves cut off near the finishing line. If you want to include an easier difficulty you either do it properly or you don't do it at all.Another minor thing that bugs me is about the "Pacifist" rank in run n' gun levels: I think that there should have been separate rankings for completing a level with an A+ and for completing it with a P. As it is, the game considers the P ranking the highest so it's pretty useless to sweat yourâ™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥â™¥trying to get an A+ when you can just go straight for a pacifist run. That's rather nonsensical since when you're doing a pacifist run you don't have to worry about time, damage or parrys, hence it's much easier to do so than to make a perfect run.Finally, bugs: there are quite a few as you can see from the discussion thread in the forums, but I personally never found gamebreaking ones. The fact that there hasn't been a single patch since the release is not comforting though, and I hope that the devs will fix some issues that are currently preventing some people from playing the game.To conclude, I know I might sound quite critical in this review, but believe me when I say that this game is absolutely amazing and that I love it with passion. It's exactly for this reason that I wanted to highlight its weak points instead of just praising it, 'cause I think that StudioMDHR guys have the potential to make even more amazing games in the future and I really want them to learn from their (overall few) errors. That said, I highly recommend everyone to play this gem, enjoy it and let yourself be amazed by the crazy world of Cuphead - even if that means you'll have to swear to your monitor a bit. It will be worth your while.

Beamex	Recommended	18.7	https://steamcommunity.com/id/Beamex/	This is a difficult game to recommend to just anyone, and there are a few things you should consider before you drop $20 on this beautifully animated and composed platformer. First thing to mention is it is rediculously hard. A player of average skill will struggle with the first few stages of this game, and if you don't handle repetitive deaths well and starting from the beggining each time, then you will want to reconsider buying this. If you are below average at games, or just platformers in general, you'll for sure want to look elsewhere as you simple will not get much value for your money.Second thing needed to know is it is "heavily focused on boss-battles" according to the steam description. I feel more needs to be said about this because it's pretty much a boss-battle game, with a very small amount of platformer levels throw in. Essentially you begin a majority of level fighting the boss and that's it. If you're expecting something like Megaman, this is not that.After all that being said, if you're still interested, then I recommend you buy this game. It brings the same sort of challenge you would expect from games like Wings of Vii, IWBTG, and Boshy. All the bosses are very unique and bring new challenges, and the controls are spot on. The parry system takes some getting used to but is very fun to use and feels great when you land them properly. There is a rating system which brings simple, classic replayability that old school gamers will enjoy, aswell as 2 player coop.My only complaint so far is how the difficulty scaled during my normal playthrough. I found that the difficulty went up very sharp towards the end of world 2, which is ok, but it dropped off at the end of world 3 and all the way towards the end of the game. Based on some world 2 bosses taking me an hour+ to beat I was expecting the final few bosses to take me days to beat, but instead they took me maybe 20 minuites each. I'm hoping expert difficulty is different.Super fun game though.

From the tigth controls to fantastic style, Cuphead has it all.Gameplay - Gameplay in Cuphead is pure joy. The controls felt great to play with, parry was a little tricky to learn, but overall the are easy to pickup. The battles are challenging but fair, making you determined to beat one boss just so you can beat another. While the game is hard it never makes you want to give up. Instead it entices you with the challenge and urges you to continue. This combined with the controls creates a wonderful experience.Design - The world is simple with four distinct sections that provide a hub to contain each boss and level. While simple it doesn't get in the way and serves its purpose well. While there only a few levels each one is different with its own elements, enemies, and challenges. The levels are built well and are entertaining to play. However the highlight of the game is not the levels but the bosses. Each one is unique and memorable, with great desgins and themes the bosses are brilliantly designed. The menus and layout is simple and easy to use, giving you everything you need. Most of the items are useful with only one or two that felt unnecessary. But overall the game is designed incredibly well.Aesthetic - What can be said that hasn't already but said before, the game is beautiful. The animation is wonderful to watch, the backgrounds are great, and the music is fantastic. Every element is perfect and provides a sense of awe and wonder.Story - The story is basic and that is the point. It gives reason to the madness, and doesn't get in the way. Nothing bad because there is nothing that can be bad.Experience - Overall the game's atmosphere is so enticing that it always leaves you wanting more. The gameplay and style tie together brilliantly and create such a satisfying experience. The difficulty builds quickly but it is never overwhelming. As a single item it succeeds in every element that brings to the table.Overall - Cuphead is easily one of the best games of 2017, and one of the best of all time. While hard it is fair, and its charm is undeniable. A truly wonderful experience-10/10

Living Joker	Recommended	9.8	https://steamcommunity.com/profiles/76561197995389078/	There's nothing I can say about this game that all the other steam reviews won't tell you, so I'll just got over the cliff's notes for you.Positives:Beautiful aesthetic that no other game has.Tight controls that mean, theoretically, all damage you take is your own fault.Challenging, almost punishing difficulty will test your patience but ultimately leave you with a sense of satisfaction.Levels are short so dying doesn't feel like that big a deal.Equipment, weapon, and super selection let you feel like you're not just playing as a specific archetype, and allow you to mix up combinations for different challenges if that's how you want to play the game.Megaman players will feel right at home with the Charge shot, knowing they need to pay attention to yet another layer of gameplay, the rhythm of charging up an attack, in order to gain a damage advantage. (If Charge is ever nerfed it will be worthless, since it is only better than other shots if you land its once-every-couple-seconds blast.)Negatives:Too many attacks don't give you any warning as to their area of effect until it occurs, making too many first tries only trial runs you know you'll fail on. (See the double flamethrower on Werner or the tugboat's chargin' mah lazor attacks for instance.)Chaser is both bad at chasing and bad at damage, and if you are even moderately skilled at moving and shooting, you'll always want the pea shooter instead for sustained rapid-fire damage.Some projectiles are difficult to see or approach from unexpected directions or far too quickly. (Bone wheel on the train boss, flames from said boss.)Unexpected interactions with various parryable items/creatures. The octopus for instance most players will assume would hurt to touch.Parrying objects above you feels off. When it's underneath you can tell when to press the button, but above it's almost like Cuphead's hitbox extends too far vertically to reliably parry anything with ensuring it will collide into you mid parry, instead of parrying as you collide into it.Short. My playtime as of my first complete Regular playthrough was 4.6 hours.Some weapons or items have limited or seemingly no worth. I used lobber once, on the bee, and didn't even need to.Scrolling in multiplayer run n' gun levels is awful, as if players are too far apart the player in the lead will often take damage before being able to dodge out of the way.All of this said, this is the first game I have paid full price for in a long time without feeling ripped off, and if you have any confidence in your hand-eye coordination I think you should give it a shot.Edit: As of the recent update supposedly the developer did indeed nerf Charge, as well as apply a few other nerfs to existing strategies. The ones which were clearly exploits like the switching weapon bug are fine, but some of them make the game a less interesting and less fun experience. This is still a thumbs up for me but less enthusiastically than before.
